# Grammar Explanations Review

## adjective_order.json

### Item 1
**English**: General order: Opinion -> Size -> Age -> Color -> Origin -> Material.

**Traditional**: ä¸€èˆ¬é †åºï¼šè§€é» -> å¤§å° -> å¹´é½¡ -> é¡è‰² -> ç”¢åœ° -> æè³ªã€‚

**Simplified**: ä¸€èˆ¬é¡ºåºï¼šè§‚ç‚¹ -> å¤§å° -> å¹´é¾„ -> é¢œè‰² -> äº§åœ° -> æè´¨ã€‚

## adjectives.json

## adverbs.json

### Item 1
**English**: Adverbs of manner usually end in -ly.

**Traditional**: å‰¯è©ç”¨æ³•ã€‚

**Simplified**: å‰¯è¯ç”¨æ³•ã€‚

---

### Item 2
**English**: Frequency adverbs go before the main verb.

**Traditional**: å‰¯è©ç”¨æ³•ã€‚

**Simplified**: å‰¯è¯ç”¨æ³•ã€‚

---

### Item 3
**English**: Adverbs modify adjectives.

**Traditional**: å‰¯è©ç”¨æ³•ã€‚

**Simplified**: å‰¯è¯ç”¨æ³•ã€‚

---

## an_a_the.json

### Item 1 (ID: apple)
**English**: # ğŸ Hey kiddos, let's explore the articles in the story!

- **an apple**: We use "an" because "apple" starts with a vowel sound.
- **the orchard**: We use "the" because it's a specific orchard where Annie lives.
- **the world**: "The" is used as we all know which world we're talking about.
- **a worm**: "A" is used because it's the first time we mention Willy the worm.
- **a river**: First time mentioning a river, so we use "a".
- **a hill**: Again, first mention, so "a".
- **the top of the hill**: We've mentioned the hill, so now it's specificâ€”use "the".
- **a tree**: First time we see the tree, so "a".
- **golden apples**: Plural noun, no article needed.
- **the sight**: Referring to that specific sight, so "the".
- **an apple**: Sharing one apple, so "an".
- **the sunset**: There's only one sunset happening, so "the".
- **the stars**: Specific stars in the sky, so "the".
- **the sky**: We all know the sky, so "the".
- **home**: "Home" doesn't need an article when referring to the concept.
- **the journey**: The specific journey they had, so "the".
- **the other apples**: Specific group of apples, so "the".
- **her stories**: Possessive "her" means no article is needed.
- **memories**: General plural noun, no article needed.

Fun, right? Now you know why those articles are used! ğŸ˜Š

### Item 2 (ID: banana)
**English**: # ğŸŒ Hey kids, let's check out the articles in this story!

- **a banana**: We use "a" because it's the first mention of Benny.
- **the best banana split**: "The" is used because it's a specific, the best one in the world.
- **a kitchen**: First time mentioning the kitchen, so "a".
- **other fruits**: Plural noun, general group, no article needed.
- **a chef**: First time we hear about the chef, so "a".
- **the kitchen**: We've mentioned it before, so it's "the" kitchen now.
- **the chef**: Referring to that specific chef, so "the".
- **a banana**: The chef picks up one banana, so "a".
- **some ice cream**: "Ice cream" is uncountable, so we use "some".
- **cherries**: Plural noun, general, no article needed.
- **the banana**: Referring to Benny specifically, so "the".
- **a bowl**: First time mentioning the bowl, so "a".
- **scoops of ice cream**: General plural, no article needed.
- **the customers**: Specific group at the restaurant, so "the".
- **the restaurant**: We know which restaurant, so "the".
- **the dessert**: Specific dessert they loved, so "the".
- **stories**: General plural noun, no article.
- **Benny's success**: Possessive noun, no article needed.
- **the other bananas**: Specific group of bananas, so "the".

Interesting, right? Articles make the story clearer! ğŸ¨

### Item 3 (ID: orange)
**English**: # ğŸŠ Hey kids, let's look at the articles in the story!

- **an orange**: "Orange" starts with a vowel sound, so we use "an".
- **a tree**: First time mentioning the tree, so "a".
- **an orchard**: "Orchard" starts with a vowel sound, so "an".
- **the sunlight**: Specific sunlight she's basking in, so "the".
- **a bird**: First mention of the bird, so "a".
- **a nest**: The bird is building one nest, first mention, so "a".
- **the tree**: We've mentioned the tree before, so "the".
- **the bird**: We know which bird now, so "the".
- **twigs and leaves**: General plural nouns, no articles needed.
- **a smile**: First time mentioning a smile, so "a".
- **a storm**: First mention of the storm, so "a".
- **the wind**: Specific wind from the storm, so "the".
- **the nest**: Specific nest we've talked about, so "the".
- **a rainbow**: First time seeing the rainbow, so "a".
- **the sky**: We all know the sky, so "the".
- **the farmer**: Specific farmer who picks the oranges, so "the".
- **the oranges**: Specific oranges on the tree, so "the".
- **a basket**: First mention of the basket, so "a".
- **other oranges**: General plural, no article needed.
- **a market**: First time mentioning the market, so "a".
- **a kind lady**: First mention of the lady, so "a".
- **delicious juice**: Uncountable noun, no article needed.
- **the lady's day**: Specific day belonging to the lady, so "the".

Fun, right? Articles help us know what we're talking about! ğŸŒˆ

**Traditional**: # ğŸŠ è¦ªæ„›çš„å°æœ‹å‹å€‘ï¼Œä¾†çœ‹çœ‹æ•…äº‹ä¸­çš„å† è©å§ï¼

**Simplified**: # ğŸŠ è¦ªçˆ±çš„å°æœ‹å‹ä»¬ï¼Œæ¥çœ‹çœ‹æ•…äº‹ä¸­çš„å† è¯å§ï¼

## articles.json

### Item 1 (ID: capybara)
**English**: **Let's Discover How 'the' Works! ğŸ­âœ¨**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a magic pointer that helps us know which special thing weâ€™re talking about. Letâ€™s check it out together!

1. **"He placed the pebble in his special spot under a big tree."**
   - **the pebble**: **â€œtheâ€** tells us itâ€™s that shiny little pebble Cappy found, not just any pebble!
   - **the river**: **â€œtheâ€** means a specific river, the one Cappy loves to play by.

2. **"The river was Cappy's favorite place."**
   - **the river**: Again, **â€œtheâ€** shows itâ€™s the same special river we talked about.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œCappy was a cute capybara,â€ here **â€œaâ€** means Cappy is just any cute capybara, not a specific one.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œa shiny pebble,â€ weâ€™re introducing it for the first time, so itâ€™s not specific yet.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œhis special spot,â€ we already know itâ€™s his spot because of **â€œhis,â€** so we donâ€™t need **â€œthe.â€**

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us point to specific, known, or unique things, making our stories clearer.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** are used to introduce new or general things that arenâ€™t specific yet.
- Words like **â€œhisâ€** or **â€œherâ€** already show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isnâ€™t needed.

Next time you read a story, try spotting where **â€œtheâ€** is used to point out special things! ğŸ‰

### Item 2 (ID: otter)
**English**: **Let's Play with How 'the' Works! ğŸ¦¦ğŸŒ³**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a little fairy that helps us know which special thing weâ€™re talking about. Letâ€™s take a look together!

1. **"Olly enjoyed sliding down the muddy banks of the stream."**
   - **the muddy banks**: **â€œtheâ€** tells us itâ€™s the specific muddy riverbank Olly likes to slide down, not just any muddy bank.
   - **the stream**: **â€œtheâ€** means a particular stream, the one in the story where Olly loves to play.

2. **"They found a hidden waterfall. The sound of the water was soothing."**
   - **the sound**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the specific sound of the water from the waterfall they found.
   - **the waterfall**: **â€œtheâ€** points to the particular waterfall they discovered.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œOlly the otter,â€ here **â€œtheâ€** is part of the name, specifically pointing to Olly.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œa shiny shell,â€ weâ€™re introducing it for the first time, so itâ€™s not specific yet.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œhis friend, Penny the panda,â€ we already know itâ€™s his friend, so **â€œtheâ€** isnâ€™t needed.

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us point to specific things, making our stories clearer and more fun.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** are used to introduce new or general things that arenâ€™t specific yet.
- Words like **â€œhisâ€** or **â€œherâ€** already show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isnâ€™t needed.

Next time you read a story, try spotting where **â€œtheâ€** is used to point out special things! ğŸŒŸ

### Item 4 (ID: panda)
**English**: **Let's Learn About 'the'! â˜€ï¸ğŸŒ³**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a little conductorâ€™s baton, helping us know which special thing weâ€™re talking about. Letâ€™s dive in!

1. **"They gathered at the sunny park."**
   - **the sunny park**: **â€œtheâ€** tells us itâ€™s that specific sunny park where they meet, not just any park.

2. **"They spread out their picnic spot under a big tree."**
   - **the picnic spot**: **â€œtheâ€** means that particular picnic spot they chose.
   - **the big tree**: **â€œtheâ€** points to the specific big tree where they set up their picnic.

3. **"They ran to find shelter under the tree."**
   - **the tree**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the same big tree they mentioned before, where they hide from the rain.

4. **"The rain stopped after a while."**
   - **the rain**: **â€œtheâ€** is talking about that specific rain that suddenly started.

5. **"The sunny park was their favorite place."**
   - **the sunny park**: **â€œtheâ€** again points to the same special park where they love to picnic.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œPenny the panda,â€ here **â€œtheâ€** is part of the name, specifically pointing to Penny.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œa big tree,â€ weâ€™re talking about any big tree for the first time.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œher friends,â€ we already know theyâ€™re her friends, so **â€œtheâ€** isnâ€™t needed.

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us know which special thing weâ€™re talking about, making our stories clearer and more fun.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** are used to introduce new or general things that arenâ€™t specific yet.
- Words like **â€œherâ€** or **â€œhisâ€** already show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isnâ€™t needed.

Next time you read a story, see if **â€œtheâ€** is pointing out something special! ğŸˆ

   - **the lantern**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the same lantern mentioned before.
   - **the garden path**: **â€œtheâ€** points to a specific path in the garden where they put the lantern.

3. **"Every evening, the lantern shone brightly."**
   - **the lantern**: Again, **â€œtheâ€** shows it's the same special lantern.

4. **"They celebrated with their friends."**
   - **the garden**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the same garden that became magical because of the lantern.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œLily the ladybug,â€ here **â€œtheâ€** is part of the name, pointing specifically to Lily.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œa small lantern,â€ we're introducing it for the first time, so it's not specific yet.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œher creation,â€ we already know it's hers, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us know which special thing we're talking about, making our stories clearer and more magical.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** introduce new or general things that aren't specific yet.
- Words like **â€œherâ€** or **â€œhisâ€** show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

Next time you read a story, see if **â€œtheâ€** is pointing out something special! ğŸŒŸ

### Item 7 (ID: mouse)
**English**: **Let's Explore 'the' Magic! âœ¨ğŸ­**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a magic wand that helps us know which special thing we're talking about. Let's see how!

1. **"He found a shiny wand in the attic."**
   - **the attic**: **â€œtheâ€** tells us it's a specific attic where Milo found the wand.

2. **"He showed the wand to his friend, Rosie the rabbit."**
   - **the wand**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the same shiny wand he found earlier.

3. **"They decided to perform a magic show."**
   - **the magic show**: **â€œtheâ€** points to the specific magic show they planned.

4. **"Suddenly, colorful lights appeared in the air."**
   - **the air**: **â€œtheâ€** means the specific air around them where the magic happened.

5. **"The magic show was a huge success."**
   - **the magic show**: Again, **â€œtheâ€** refers to their special show.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œMilo the mouse,â€ here **â€œtheâ€** is part of the name, specifically pointing to Milo.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œa shiny wand,â€ we're introducing it for the first time, so it's not specific yet.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œhis tiny home,â€ we already know it's his home, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us know which special thing we're talking about, making our stories clearer and more magical.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** introduce new or general things that aren't specific yet.
- Words like **â€œhisâ€** or **â€œherâ€** show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

Next time you read a story, see if **â€œtheâ€** is pointing out something special! ğŸŒŸ

### Item 8 (ID: tiger)
**English**: **Let's Explore 'the' Treasure! ğŸï¸ğŸ’**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a map guiding us to know which special thing we're talking about. Let's see how!

   - **the tall mountains**: **â€œtheâ€** means those specific mountains they climbed.

   - **the soft ground**: **â€œtheâ€** indicates the specific ground at the treasure spot.

6. **"Inside the chest, there were shiny gems and gold coins."**
   - **the chest**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the specific chest they found.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œTina the tiger,â€ here **â€œtheâ€** is part of the name, specifically pointing to Tina.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œan old map,â€ we're introducing it for the first time, so it's not specific yet.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œher friend, Benny the bird,â€ we already know it's her friend, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** introduce new or general things that aren't specific yet.
- Words like **â€œherâ€** or **â€œhisâ€** show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

### Item 9 (ID: fox)
**English**: **Let's See 'the' Magic! ğŸ¦ŠğŸ²**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a little magician helping us know which special thing we're talking about. Let's explore!

1. **"Freddy gathered fresh vegetables from the garden."**
   - **the garden**: **â€œtheâ€** tells us it's a specific garden where Freddy got the veggies.

2. **"He also collected juicy berries from the bushes."**
   - **the bushes**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to specific bushes where he picked berries.

3. **"They prepared a big table under the old oak tree."**
   - **the old oak tree**: **â€œtheâ€** points to a specific tree where they set up.

4. **"When the feast was ready, all the friends came."**
   - **the feast**: **â€œtheâ€** means the specific feast they prepared.

5. **"They danced and laughed under the twinkling stars."**
   - **the twinkling stars**: **â€œtheâ€** indicates the specific stars above them.

6. **"The old oak tree was filled with joy and friendship."**
   - **the old oak tree**: Again, **â€œtheâ€** shows it's the same special tree.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **General Description**: Like â€œFreddy the fox,â€ here **â€œtheâ€** is part of the name, pointing specifically to Freddy.
- **First Mention**: When we say â€œa big table,â€ we're introducing it for the first time, so it's not specific yet.
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œhis friends,â€ we already know they're his friends, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us know which special thing we're talking about, making our stories clearer and more delightful.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** introduce new or general things that aren't specific yet.
- Words like **â€œhisâ€** or **â€œherâ€** show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

Next time you read a story, see if **â€œtheâ€** is pointing out something special! ğŸŒŸ

### Item 10 (ID: hedgehog)
**English**: **Let's Explore 'the' Magic! ğŸ¦”ğŸŒ»**

In this story, **â€œtheâ€** is like a little compass pointing to specific things. Let's see how!

1. **"They decided to play in the big garden."**
   - **the big garden**: **â€œtheâ€** tells us it's a specific big garden where they chose to play.

2. **"Hugo rolled into a tight ball under the bushes."**
   - **the bushes**: **â€œtheâ€** refers to the specific bushes where Hugo hid.

3. **"Charlie climbed up the tall sunflower."**
   - **the tall sunflower**: **â€œtheâ€** points to a specific tall sunflower where Charlie hid.

4. **"He searched behind the rocks and near the trees."**
   - **the rocks** and **the trees**: **â€œtheâ€** indicates specific rocks and trees where Hugo looked.

5. **"The big garden was the perfect place for their games."**
   - **the big garden**: Again, **â€œtheâ€** refers to the same garden.

**Why Donâ€™t Other Nouns Use â€œtheâ€?**

- **First Mention**: In â€œa hole in the ground,â€ it's the first time we mention it, so we use **â€œa.â€**
- **Possessive or Pronouns**: In â€œhis friends,â€ **â€œhisâ€** shows ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

**In Summary!**

- **â€œtheâ€** helps us point out specific things, making the story clearer.
- **â€œaâ€** and **â€œanâ€** introduce new things.
- **Possessive words** (like his, her) show ownership, so **â€œtheâ€** isn't needed.

Try finding what specific things **â€œtheâ€** points to in the story! ğŸŒŸ

**Traditional**: **ä¸€èµ·ä¾†æ¢ç´¢ã€Œtheã€çš„é­”æ³•å§ï¼ğŸ¦”ğŸŒ»**

### Item 11 (ID: koala)
**English**: **Learn 'the' with Kevin the Koala! ğŸ¨ğŸƒ**

1. **the eucalyptus tree**: Referring to the specific tree where Kevin naps.
2. **the perfect branch**: The specific branch Kevin found for his nap.
3. **the gardener**: A specific person known in the story.
4. **the bushes**: The particular plants being trimmed.
5. **the wind** and **the leaves**: Specific natural elements in the scene.

**Tip**: We use **â€œtheâ€** when referring to specific or previously mentioned things in a story!

**Traditional**: **å’Œç„¡å°¾ç†Š Kevin ä¸€èµ·å­¸ã€Œtheã€ï¼ğŸ¨ğŸƒ**

4. **the bushes**ï¼šæŒ‡åœ’ä¸æ­£åœ¨ä¿®å‰ªçš„é‚£äº›çŒæœ¨ã€‚
5. **the wind** å’Œ **the leaves**ï¼šç‰¹å®šçš„é¢¨å’Œç‰¹å®šçš„è‘‰å­è²ã€‚

**å°è²¼å£«**ï¼šç•¶æˆ‘å€‘åœ¨è«‡è«–æ•…äº‹ä¸­å·²ç¶“å‡ºç¾æˆ–ç‰¹å®šçš„äº‹ç‰©æ™‚ï¼Œå°±æœƒç”¨åˆ° **ã€Œtheã€**ï¼

**Simplified**: **å’Œè€ƒæ‹‰ Kevin ä¸€èµ·å­¦â€œtheâ€ï¼ğŸ¨ğŸƒ**

1. **the eucalyptus tree**ï¼šæŒ‡ç‰¹å®šçš„æ¡‰æ ‘ï¼Œå°±æ˜¯ Kevin ç¡è§‰çš„é‚£ä¸€æ£µã€‚

### Item 12 (ID: kangaroo)
**English**: **Kira the Kangaroo's Big Hop! ğŸ¦˜ğŸŒ¾**

### Item 13 (ID: penguin)
**English**: **Pip the Penguin's Icy Slide! ğŸ§â„ï¸**

1. **the icy shore**: The specific cold shore where Pip lives.
2. **the freezing ocean**: The particular sea where penguins swim.
3. **the snow**: The specific white snow on the ground.
4. **the ice block**: The particular large piece of ice Pip found.
5. **the stars** and **the colony**: Specific lights in the sky and the group of penguins.

**Think**: Why not "a"? Because we are pointing to a specific shore and ice block!

## be_verb_adjectives.json

### Item 1 (ID: feelings)
**English**: # My Feelings

When describing feelings or states with adjectives, you MUST use a **Be Verb (am/is/are)**. You cannot skip it!

1. **[am]**: I am happy.
2. **[is]**: My brother (He) is sad.
3. **[are]**: My parents (They) are proud.
4. **[are]**: We are happy.
5. **[is]**: My sister (She) is excited.
6. **[am]**: I am not angry.
7. **[are]**: You are my best friend.
8. **[are]**: They are kind.

Remember: Don't say "I very busy". Say "I **am** very busy".

**Traditional**: # æˆ‘çš„å¿ƒæƒ…

æè¿°å¿ƒæƒ…æˆ–ç‹€æ…‹æ™‚ï¼Œå¿…é ˆè¦æœ‰ **Beå‹•è© (am/is/are)**ï¼Œä¸èƒ½çœç•¥å–”ï¼

1. **[am]**ï¼šI am happy. (æˆ‘å¾ˆå¿«æ¨‚)
2. **[is]**ï¼šMy brother (He) is sad. (ä»–å¾ˆé›£é)
3. **[are]**ï¼šMy parents (They) are proud. (ä»–å€‘å¾ˆé©•å‚²)
4. **[are]**ï¼šWe are happy. (æˆ‘å€‘å¾ˆå¿«æ¨‚)
5. **[is]**ï¼šMy sister (She) is excited. (å¥¹å¾ˆèˆˆå¥®)
6. **[am]**ï¼šI am not angry. (æˆ‘ä¸ç”Ÿæ°£)
7. **[are]**ï¼šYou are my best friend. (ä½ æ˜¯æˆ‘çš„å¥½æœ‹å‹)
8. **[are]**ï¼šThey are kind. (ä»–å€‘å¾ˆä»æ…ˆ)

è¨˜ä½ï¼šä¸­æ–‡é›–ç„¶èªªã€Œæˆ‘å¾ˆå¿™ã€ï¼Œè‹±æ–‡è¦èªª "I **am** very busy"ã€‚

**Simplified**: # æˆ‘çš„å¿ƒæƒ…

æè¿°å¿ƒæƒ…æˆ–çŠ¶æ€æ—¶ï¼Œå¿…é¡»è¦æœ‰ **BeåŠ¨è¯ (am/is/are)**ï¼Œä¸èƒ½çœç•¥å–”ï¼

1. **[am]**ï¼šI am happy. (æˆ‘å¾ˆå¿«ä¹)
2. **[is]**ï¼šMy brother (He) is sad. (ä»–å¾ˆéš¾è¿‡)
3. **[are]**ï¼šMy parents (They) are proud. (ä»–ä»¬å¾ˆéª„å‚²)
4. **[are]**ï¼šWe are happy. (æˆ‘ä»¬å¾ˆå¿«ä¹)
5. **[is]**ï¼šMy sister (She) is excited. (å¥¹å¾ˆå…´å¥‹)
6. **[am]**ï¼šI am not angry. (æˆ‘ä¸ç”Ÿæ°”)
7. **[are]**ï¼šYou are my best friend. (ä½ æ˜¯æˆ‘çš„å¥½æœ‹å‹)
8. **[are]**ï¼šThey are kind. (ä»–ä»¬å¾ˆä»æ…ˆ)

è®°ä½ï¼šä¸­æ–‡è™½ç„¶è¯´â€œæˆ‘å¾ˆå¿™â€ï¼Œè‹±æ–‡è¦è¯´ "I **am** very busy"ã€‚

### Item 2 (ID: weather)
**English**: # The Weather

Use **am**, **is**, or **are** to connect the subject to the adjective.

1. **[is]**: The sun (It) is bright.
2. **[is]**: The sky (It) is blue.
3. **[are]**: The clouds (They) are white.
4. **[am]**: I am hot.
5. **[is]**: The water (It) is cold.
6. **[are]**: The trees (They) are tall.
7. **[is]**: It is a beautiful day.
8. **[is]**: The wind (It) is strong.
9. **[are]**: We are ready.

4. **[am]**ï¼šI am hot. (æˆ‘è¦ºå¾—ç†±)
5. **[is]**ï¼šThe water (It) is cold. (æ°´å¾ˆå†·)
6. **[are]**ï¼šThe trees (They) are tall. (æ¨¹å¾ˆé«˜)
7. **[is]**ï¼šIt is a beautiful day. (ä»Šå¤©æ˜¯ç¾å¥½çš„ä¸€å¤©)

### Item 3 (ID: house)
**English**: # My House

Connect the subject to its description with a Be Verb.

1. **[is]**: My house (It) is small.
2. **[are]**: The walls (They) are yellow.
3. **[is]**: The kitchen (It) is clean.
4. **[is]**: My bedroom (It) is messy.
5. **[are]**: The windows (They) are big.
6. **[is]**: The garden (It) is beautiful.
7. **[are]**: Neighbors (They) are friendly.
8. **[is]**: My dog (It) is cute.
9. **[am]**: I am safe.
10. **[are]**: We are lucky.

### Item 4 (ID: classroom)
**English**: # The Classroom

English sentences need a verb. Adjectives describe the subject, but the Be Verb connects them.

1. **[is]**: Classroom (It) is noisy.
2. **[are]**: Students (They) are loud.
3. **[is]**: Teacher (He/She) is patient.
4. **[is]**: Chalkboard (It) is green.
5. **[are]**: Desks (They) are old.
6. **[are]**: Books (They) are heavy.
7. **[am]**: I am tired.
8. **[is]**: Pencil (It) is sharp.
9. **[is]**: Test (It) is difficult.
10. **[are]**: We are smart.

**Traditional**: # æ•™å®¤è£¡

ä¸­æ–‡å¸¸èªªã€Œé€™æ•™å®¤å¾ˆåµã€ï¼Œè‹±æ–‡ä¸€å®šè¦èªª "This classroom **is** noisy"ã€‚

1. **[is]**ï¼šClassroom (It) is noisy.
2. **[are]**ï¼šStudents (They) are loud.
3. **[is]**ï¼šTeacher (He/She) is patient.
4. **[is]**ï¼šChalkboard (It) is green.
5. **[are]**ï¼šDesks (They) are old.
6. **[are]**ï¼šBooks (They) are heavy.
7. **[am]**ï¼šI am tired.
8. **[is]**ï¼šPencil (It) is sharp.
9. **[is]**ï¼šTest (It) is difficult.
10. **[are]**ï¼šWe are smart.

**Simplified**: # æ•™å®¤é‡Œ

ä¸­æ–‡å¸¸è¯´â€œè¿™æ•™å®¤å¾ˆåµâ€ï¼Œè‹±æ–‡ä¸€å®šè¦è¯´ "This classroom **is** noisy"ã€‚

1. **[is]**ï¼šClassroom (It) is noisy.
2. **[are]**ï¼šStudents (They) are loud.
3. **[is]**ï¼šTeacher (He/She) is patient.
4. **[is]**ï¼šChalkboard (It) is green.
5. **[are]**ï¼šDesks (They) are old.
6. **[are]**ï¼šBooks (They) are heavy.

### Item 5 (ID: people)
**English**: # Describing People

Don't forget the Be Verb when describing people's characteristics.

1. **[is]**: Father (He) is tall.
2. **[is]**: Mother (She) is beautiful.
3. **[are]**: You are funny.
4. **[am]**: I am serious.
5. **[are]**: They are famous.
6. **[is]**: Baby (He/She) is sleepy.
7. **[is]**: Hair (It) is long.
8. **[are]**: Eyes (They) are blue.
9. **[are]**: We are strong.
10. **[is]**: She is rich.

**Traditional**: # æè¿°äººç‰©

2. **[is]**ï¼šMother (She) is beautiful.
3. **[are]**ï¼šYou are funny.
4. **[am]**ï¼šI am serious.
5. **[are]**ï¼šThey are famous.
6. **[is]**ï¼šBaby (He/She) is sleepy.
7. **[is]**ï¼šHair (It) is long. (é ­é«®è¦–ç‚ºå–®æ•¸ä¸å¯æ•¸)
8. **[are]**ï¼šEyes (They) are blue. (çœ¼ç›é€šå¸¸æ˜¯è¤‡æ•¸)
9. **[are]**ï¼šWe are strong.

**Simplified**: # æè¿°äººç‰©

2. **[is]**ï¼šMother (She) is beautiful.
3. **[are]**ï¼šYou are funny.

## conditionals.json

### Item 1 (ID: if-i-were-rich)
**English**: # ğŸ’­ If I Were Rich (Conditionals)

1. **First Conditional (Real Future)**: If it rains, I **[will stay]** home.
2. **Second Conditional (Hypothetical)**: If I **[won]** (imaginary past form), I would buy...
   - If I **[were]** you...
3. **Third Conditional (Regret)**: If I had studied, I **[would have passed]**.
4. **Zero Conditional (Facts)**: Water **[boils]** at 100 degrees.

**Traditional**: # ğŸ’­ å¦‚æœæˆ‘æ˜¯æœ‰éŒ¢äºº (Conditionals)

æ¢ä»¶å¥ (Conditionals) æœ‰ä¸åŒçš„é¡å‹ï¼š

1. **First Conditional (çœŸå¯¦æœªä¾†)**: If + Present, will + Verb.
   - If it rains, I **[will stay]** home.
2. **Second Conditional (èˆ‡ç¾åœ¨äº‹å¯¦ç›¸å)**: If + Past, would + Verb.
   - If I **[won]** (å‡è¨­ä¸­) the lottery, I would buy...
   - If I **[were]** you (å‡è¨­æˆ‘æ˜¯ä½ )...
3. **Third Conditional (èˆ‡éå»äº‹å¯¦ç›¸å)**: If + Past Perfect, would have + PP.
   - If I had studied, I **[would have passed]**.
4. **Zero Conditional (çœŸç†)**: If + Present, Present.
   - Water **[boils]** if it reaches 100 degrees.

**Simplified**: # ğŸ’­ å¦‚æœæˆ‘æ˜¯æœ‰é’±äºº (Conditionals)

æ¡ä»¶å¥ (Conditionals) æœ‰ä¸åŒçš„ç±»å‹ï¼š

1. **First Conditional (çœŸå®æœªæ¥)**: If + Present, will + Verb.
   - If it rains, I **[will stay]** home.
2. **Second Conditional (ä¸ç°åœ¨äº‹å®ç›¸å)**: If + Past, would + Verb.
   - If I **[won]** (å‡è®¾ä¸­) the lottery, I would buy...
   - If I **[were]** you (å‡è®¾æˆ‘æ˜¯ä½ )...
3. **Third Conditional (ä¸è¿‡å»äº‹å®ç›¸å)**: If + Past Perfect, would have + PP.
   - If I had studied, I **[would have passed]**.
4. **Zero Conditional (çœŸç†)**: If + Present, Present.
   - Water **[boils]** if it reaches 100 degrees.

## gerunds_infinitives.json

### Item 1 (ID: hobbies)
**English**: # ğŸŠ Hobbies and Habits (Gerunds vs Infinitives)

1. **enjoy + ing**: enjoy **[swimming]**.
2. **decide + to**: decided **[to go]**.
3. **stop + ing**: Quit an action (quit smoking).
4. **stop + to**: Pause to do something (pouse to smoke).
5. **promise + to**: promised **[to help]**.
6. **finish + ing**: finished **[reading]**.
7. **look forward to + ing**: 'to' is a preposition here.

**Traditional**: # ğŸŠ èˆˆè¶£èˆ‡ç¿’æ…£ (Gerunds vs Infinitives)

å‹•åè© (V-ing) èˆ‡ ä¸å®šè© (to V) çš„ç”¨æ³•é€šå¸¸éœ€è¦è¨˜æ†¶ã€‚

1. **enjoy + V-ing**: I enjoy **[swimming]**.
2. **decide + to V**: I decided **[to go]**.
3. **stop + V-ing**: åœæ­¢åšæŸäº‹ (æˆ’è¸) -> stop **[smoking]**.
4. **stop + to V**: åœä¸‹ä¾†ã€Œç‚ºäº†ã€å»åšæŸäº‹ -> stop **[to smoke]**.
5. **promise + to V**: promised **[to help]**.
6. **finish + V-ing**: finished **[reading]**.
7. **look forward to + V-ing**: é€™è£¡çš„ to æ˜¯ä»‹ç³»è©ï¼Œå¾Œæ¥ V-ing -> to **[seeing]**.

**Simplified**: # ğŸŠ å…´è¶£ä¸ä¹ æƒ¯ (Gerunds vs Infinitives)

åŠ¨åè¯ (V-ing) ä¸ ä¸å®šè¯ (to V) çš„ç”¨æ³•é€šå¸¸éœ€è¦è®°å¿†ã€‚

1. **enjoy + V-ing**: I enjoy **[swimming]**.
2. **decide + to V**: I decided **[to go]**.
3. **stop + V-ing**: åœæ­¢åšæŸäº‹ (æˆ’çƒŸ) -> stop **[smoking]**.
4. **stop + to V**: åœä¸‹æ¥â€œä¸ºäº†â€å»åšæŸäº‹ -> stop **[to smoke]**.
5. **promise + to V**: promised **[to help]**.
6. **finish + V-ing**: finished **[reading]**.
7. **look forward to + V-ing**: è¿™é‡Œçš„ to æ˜¯ä»‹ç³»è¯ï¼Œåæ¥ V-ing -> to **[seeing]**.

## modals.json

### Item 1 (ID: project-deadline)
**English**: # ğŸ—“ï¸ Project Deadline (Modals)

Modals express obligation, possibility, and politeness.

1. **[must]**: Obligation.
2. **[might]**: Possibility.
3. **[Could]**: Polite request.
4. **[must]**: Logic deduction.
5. **[should]**: Advice.
6. **[can't]**: Logical impossibility.

**Traditional**: # ğŸ—“ï¸ å°ˆæ¡ˆæˆªæ­¢æ—¥ (Modals)

3. **[Could]**: ç¦®è²Œè«‹æ±‚ (Polite request)ã€‚
4. **[must]**: é«˜åº¦è‚¯å®šæ¨æ¸¬ (90-100%)ã€‚
5. **[should]**: å»ºè­° (Advice)ã€‚
6. **[can't]**: ä¸å¯èƒ½ (Impossibility)ã€‚

**Simplified**: # ğŸ—“ï¸ ä¸“æ¡ˆæˆªæ­¢æ—¥ (Modals)

åŠ©åŠ¨è¯ (Modals) è¡¨è¾¾è¯­æ°”ã€å¯èƒ½æ€§å’Œç¤¼è²Œã€‚

1. **[must]**: å¼ºåˆ¶æ€§ (Mandatory)ã€‚

## passive_voice.json

### Item 1 (ID: mistake)
**English**: # ğŸ›ï¸ The Mistake (Passive Voice)

Use **Be + Past Participle** when the focus is on the object, not the doer.

1. **[was made]**: A mistake was made.
2. **[was written]**: Report was written.
3. **[was built]**: House was built.
4. **[is spoken]**: English is spoken.
5. **[was caught]**: Thief was caught.
6. **[was painted]**: It was painted.

4. **[is spoken]**: è‹±èªã€Œè¢«ã€èªª (ç¾åœ¨äº‹å¯¦)ã€‚

## present_perfect.json

### Item 1 (ID: lost-keys)
**English**: # ğŸ”‘ Lost Keys (Present Perfect vs. Past Simple)

The key to distinguishing them is:
1. Does it affect 'now'?
2. Is the time 'finished' (yesterday, last year)?

1. **[have lost]**: Keys are still lost now. (Present relevance)
2. **[lost]**: happened Yesterday (Finished time).
3. **[have visited]**: Life experience (Unfinished time frame).
4. **[visited]**: happened Last year (Finished time).
5. **[have lived]**: Started in past, continues now.
6. **[lived]**: Lived in past, not anymore.
7. **[has finished]**: Just finished (Connection to now).
8. **[finished]**: An hour ago (Finished time).

**Traditional**: # ğŸ”‘ éºå¤±çš„é‘°åŒ™ (ç¾åœ¨å®Œæˆå¼ vs éå»å¼)

åˆ†è¾¨ **Present Perfect** (ç¾åœ¨å®Œæˆå¼) å’Œ **Past Simple** (éå»ç°¡å–®å¼) çš„é—œéµåœ¨æ–¼ï¼š
1. å‹•ä½œæ˜¯å¦å°ã€Œç¾åœ¨ã€æœ‰å½±éŸ¿ï¼Ÿ
2. æ™‚é–“æ˜¯å¦æ˜¯ã€Œæ˜ç¢ºçš„éå»ã€ (å¦‚ yesterday, last year)ï¼Ÿ

1. **[have lost]**ï¼šé‘°åŒ™ä¸è¦‹äº†ï¼Œç¾åœ¨é‚„æ²’æ‰¾åˆ° (å½±éŸ¿ç¾åœ¨)ã€‚
2. **[lost]**ï¼šæ˜¨å¤©ç™¼ç”Ÿçš„äº‹ (Yesterday)ï¼Œå·²ç¶“çµæŸã€‚
3. **[have visited]**ï¼šäººç”Ÿç¶“é©—ï¼Œæ™‚é–“ä¸æ˜ç¢º (in my life)ã€‚
4. **[visited]**ï¼šå»å¹´ç™¼ç”Ÿçš„äº‹ (Last year)ã€‚
5. **[have lived]**ï¼šå¾éå»æŒçºŒåˆ°ç¾åœ¨ (for ten years)ï¼Œé‚„ä½åœ¨é€™è£¡ã€‚
6. **[lived]**ï¼šä»¥å‰ä½åœ¨å€«æ•¦ï¼Œç¾åœ¨ä¸ä½äº† (Before that)ã€‚
7. **[has finished]**ï¼šå‰›å‰›å®Œæˆ (just now)ï¼Œå¼·èª¿å®Œæˆçš„ç‹€æ…‹ã€‚
8. **[finished]**ï¼šä¸€å°æ™‚å‰å®Œæˆ (an hour ago)ï¼Œæ˜ç¢ºçš„éå»æ™‚é–“ã€‚

**Simplified**: # ğŸ”‘ é—å¤±çš„é’¥åŒ™ (ç°åœ¨å®Œæˆå¼ vs è¿‡å»å¼)

åˆ†è¾¨ **Present Perfect** (ç°åœ¨å®Œæˆå¼) å’Œ **Past Simple** (è¿‡å»ç®€å•å¼) çš„å…³éµåœ¨æ–¼ï¼š
1. åŠ¨ä½œæ˜¯å¦å¯¹ã€Œç°åœ¨ã€æœ‰å½±éŸ¿ï¼Ÿ
2. æ—¶é—´æ˜¯å¦æ˜¯ã€Œæ˜ç¡®çš„è¿‡å»ã€ (å¦‚ yesterday, last year)ï¼Ÿ

1. **[have lost]**ï¼šé’¥åŒ™ä¸è§äº†ï¼Œç°åœ¨é‚„æ²¡æ‰¾åˆ° (å½±éŸ¿ç°åœ¨)ã€‚
2. **[lost]**ï¼šæ˜¨å¤©ç™¼ç”Ÿçš„äº‹ (Yesterday)ï¼Œå·²ç¶“çµæŸã€‚
3. **[have visited]**ï¼šäººç”Ÿç¶“éªŒï¼Œæ—¶é—´ä¸æ˜ç¡® (in my life)ã€‚
4. **[visited]**ï¼šå»å¹´ç™¼ç”Ÿçš„äº‹ (Last year)ã€‚
5. **[have lived]**ï¼šå¾è¿‡å»æŒçºŒåˆ°ç°åœ¨ (for ten years)ï¼Œé‚„ä½åœ¨è¿™è£¡ã€‚
6. **[lived]**ï¼šä»¥å‰ä½åœ¨ä¼¦æ•¦ï¼Œç°åœ¨ä¸ä½äº† (Before that)ã€‚

## pronouns.json

### Item 1 (ID: family)

## question_formation.json

### Item 1 (ID: q1)
**English**: English questions require changing the word order.
1. Move the Be verb (am, is, are) or auxiliary verb (can, will) before the subject.
   e.g., You are ready. -> Are you ready?
2. For other verbs, use the auxiliary 'Do' or 'Does' at the beginning.
   e.g., You like this. -> Do you like this?
3. Question words (Where, What, How) always go at the very front.
   e.g., Where are you going?

**Traditional**: è‹±æ–‡ç–‘å•å¥éœ€è¦èª¿æ•´èªåºã€‚
1. Beå‹•è© (am, is, are) æˆ–åŠ©å‹•è© (can, will) è¦ç§»åˆ°ä¸»è©å‰é¢ã€‚
   ä¾‹å¦‚: You are ready. -> Are you ready?
2. ä¸€èˆ¬å‹•è©ç–‘å•å¥éœ€åœ¨å¥é¦–åŠ åŠ©å‹•è© Do/Doesã€‚
   ä¾‹å¦‚: You like this. -> Do you like this?
3. ç–‘å•è© (Where, What, How) æ°¸é æ”¾åœ¨å¥é¦–ã€‚
   ä¾‹å¦‚: Where are you going?

**Simplified**: è‹±æ–‡ç–‘é—®å¥éœ€è¦è°ƒæ•´è¯­åºã€‚
1. BeåŠ¨è¯ (am, is, are) æˆ–åŠ©åŠ¨è¯ (can, will) è¦ç§»åˆ°ä¸»è¯å‰é¢ã€‚
   ä¾‹å¦‚: You are ready. -> Are you ready?
2. ä¸€èˆ¬åŠ¨è¯ç–‘é—®å¥éœ€åœ¨å¥é¦–åŠ åŠ©åŠ¨è¯ Do/Doesã€‚
   ä¾‹å¦‚: You like this. -> Do you like this?
3. ç–‘é—®è¯ (Where, What, How) æ°¸é æ”¾åœ¨å¥é¦–ã€‚
   ä¾‹å¦‚: Where are you going?

---

### Item 2 (ID: q2)
**English**: Even with question words (When, Why, How, What, Who), the auxiliary verb must come before the subject.
e.g., Why did he leave? (Correct)
Why he left? (Incorrect - missing auxiliary inversion)

**Traditional**: å³ä½¿æœ‰ç–‘å•è© (When, Why, How, What, Who)ï¼ŒåŠ©å‹•è©ä¾ç„¶è¦æ”¾åœ¨ä¸»è©å‰é¢ã€‚
ä¾‹å¦‚: Why did he leave? (æ­£ç¢º)
Why he left? (éŒ¯èª¤ - ç¼ºå°‘åŠ©å‹•è©å€’è£)

**Simplified**: å³ä½¿æœ‰ç–‘é—®è¯ (When, Why, How, What, Who)ï¼ŒåŠ©åŠ¨è¯ä¾ç„¶è¦æ”¾åœ¨ä¸»è¯å‰é¢ã€‚
ä¾‹å¦‚: Why did he leave? (æ­£ç¡®)
Why he left? (é”™èª¤ - ç¼ºå°‘åŠ©åŠ¨è¯å€’è£)

### Item 3 (ID: q3)
**English**: Start with Do/Does for simple present questions.

**Traditional**: Yes/No questions with regular verbs need Do/Does at the start.

**Simplified**: Yes/No questions with regular verbs need Do/Does at the start.

**Simplified**: Wh- words + Do/Does + Subject + Verb.

**Simplified**: Past questions use 'Did' + base verb.

**Simplified**: Will + Subject + Verb. Don't forget 'be' if there's no action verb!

**Simplified**: Modal verbs (Can, Could) move to the front.

**Simplified**: Be verbs (Is, Are, Am) move to the front.

**Simplified**: Question word + Be verb + Subject + V-ing.

## relative_clauses.json

### Item 1 (ID: the-man-who)
**English**: # ğŸ”— The Man Who... (Relative Clauses)

Relative pronouns link details to the noun.

1. **[who]**: For people.
2. **[that]**: For things (identifying).
3. **[whose]**: For possession (her brother).
4. **[where]**: For places.
5. **[which]**: For things (extra info with comma).
6. **[who]**: For people.

**Traditional**: # ğŸ”— é‚£å€‹...çš„äºº (Relative Clauses)

é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©ç”¨ä¾†å½¢å®¹å…ˆè¡Œè©ï¼š

1. **[who]**: å½¢å®¹**äºº** (man)ã€‚
2. **[that]**: å½¢å®¹**äº‹ç‰©** (book) (which ä¹Ÿå¯ä»¥ï¼Œä½†åœ¨é™å®šç”¨æ³• that å¸¸ç”¨)ã€‚
3. **[whose]**: å½¢å®¹**æ‰€æœ‰æ ¼** (girl's brother)ã€‚
4. **[where]**: å½¢å®¹**åœ°é»** (cafe)ã€‚
5. **[which]**: å½¢å®¹**äº‹ç‰©** (phone)ï¼Œé€—è™Ÿå¾Œéé™å®šç”¨æ³•ä¸å¯ç”¨ thatã€‚
6. **[who]**: å½¢å®¹**äºº** (person)ã€‚

**Simplified**: # ğŸ”— é‚£ä¸ª...çš„äºº (Relative Clauses)

å…³ç³»ä»£åè¯ç”¨æ¥å½¢å®¹å…ˆè¡Œè¯ï¼š

1. **[who]**: å½¢å®¹**äºº** (man)ã€‚
2. **[that]**: å½¢å®¹**äº‹ç‰©** (book) (which ä¹Ÿå¯ä»¥ï¼Œä½†åœ¨é™å®šç”¨æ³• that å¸¸ç”¨)ã€‚
3. **[whose]**: å½¢å®¹**æ‰€æœ‰æ ¼** (girl's brother)ã€‚
4. **[where]**: å½¢å®¹**åœ°ç‚¹** (cafe)ã€‚
5. **[which]**: å½¢å®¹**äº‹ç‰©** (phone)ï¼Œé€—è™Ÿåéé™å®šç”¨æ³•ä¸å¯ç”¨ thatã€‚
6. **[who]**: å½¢å®¹**äºº** (person)ã€‚

## singular.json

### Item 1 (ID: dragon)
**English**: # ğŸ² Dear little adventurers, let's explore the nouns!

- **[forest|forests]**: With "a" before, only singular **forest** is correct.
- **[dragon|dragons]**: Only one dragon, so we use singular **dragon**.
- **[gems|gem]** and **[herbs|herb]**: He collected many, so plural **gems** and **herbs** are correct.
- **[owl|owls]**: "a" indicates singular, so we use **owl**.
- **[treasure|treasures]**: "a hidden" requires singular **treasure**.
- **[adventure|adventures]**: "an" before it means singular **adventure**.
- **[ruin-ruins]** and **[cave-caves]**: Both forms are acceptable; they could explore one or many.
- **[challenges|challenge]**: "many" needs plural **challenges**.
- **[one|ones]**: "each" is followed by singular **one**.
- **[journey-journeys]**: Both forms work; they might have had one or multiple journeys.
- **[artifact|artifacts]**: "a" requires singular **artifact**.
- **[wish-wishes]**: Both forms are acceptable; the artifact could grant one or many wishes.
- **[kingdom-kingdoms]**: Both forms work, depending on whether peace is wished for one or multiple kingdoms.
- **[story-stories]**: Both forms are correct; he may have shared one or many stories.
- **[friends|friend]**: Since it says "them," plural **friends** is correct.
- **[adventure-adventures]**: Both forms are acceptable; they could seek one or multiple adventures.
- **[treasures|treasure]**: "are" indicates plural, so **treasures** is correct.
- **[memory-memories]** and **[friendship-friendships]**: Both forms work, depending on emphasis on singular or multiple memories and friendships.

### Item 2 (ID: goblin)
**English**: # ğŸ§™â€â™‚ï¸ Hey pals, let's check out the nouns!

- **[village|villages]**: Only one village, so singular **village** is correct.
- **[goblin|goblins]**: Gizmo is one goblin, so we use singular **goblin**.
- **[neighbors|neighbor]**: He plays pranks on many, so plural **neighbors**.
- **[shoes|shoe]** and **[noses|nose]**: Plural because he hides multiple shoes and tickles multiple noses.
- **[map|maps]**: He found one map, so singular **map**.
- **[tunnel-tunnels]**: Both forms work; he could have entered one or many tunnels.
- **[toys-toy]** and **[candies-candy]**: Both acceptable; he found one or many.
- **[treasures-treasure]**: Both forms are correct; he shared one or multiple treasures.
- **[community|communities]**: Refers to one community, so singular **community**.
- **[heart|hearts]**: He is known for one generous heart, so singular **heart**.

### Item 3 (ID: unicorn)
**English**: # ğŸ¦„ Hello little dreamers, let's explore nouns together!

- **[meadow|meadows]**: Only one meadow, so singular **meadow**.
- **[unicorn|unicorns]**: Luna is one unicorn, so singular **unicorn**.

- **[shadows|shadow]** and **[puzzles|puzzle]**: Plural **shadows** and **puzzles** because they face many.
- **[friends-friend]**: Both forms are acceptable; they become best friends or best friend.
- **[flowers-flower]**: The fairy gifts her one or multiple flowers; both are correct.
- **[night-nights]**: The flowers bloom every night or nights; both forms work.

- **[flowers-flower]**ï¼šä»™å¥³é€ç»™å¥¹èŠ±æœµï¼Œå¯èƒ½æ˜¯ä¸€æœµæˆ–å¤šæœµï¼Œä¸¤ç§å½¢å¼éƒ½è¡Œã€‚

### Item 4 (ID: troll)
**English**: # ğŸ§â€â™‚ï¸ Greetings, young scholars! Let's see the magic of nouns!

- **[bridge|bridges]**: Only one bridge, so singular **bridge**.
- **[troll|trolls]**: Tobias is one troll, so singular **troll**.
- **[trolls|troll]**: Referring to other trolls, so plural **trolls**.
- **[books|book]** and **[riddles|riddle]**: Plural because he reads and solves many.
- **[advice|advices]**: "advice" is uncountable, so singular form.
- **[questions-question]**: Both forms are acceptable; travelers may ask one or many questions.
- **[knowledge|knowledges]**: "knowledge" is uncountable, so singular.
- **[friends-friend]**: Both forms work; he makes new friend or friends.
- **[knight|knights]**: He taught one knight, so singular **knight**.
- **[courage|courages]**: "courage" is uncountable, so singular.
- **[land-lands]**: Both forms are acceptable; spreading kindness throughout one or multiple lands.

Neat, huh? ğŸ“–

### Item 5 (ID: fairy)
**English**: # ğŸ§šâ€â™€ï¸ Hey little fairies, let's check out the nouns!

- **[grove|groves]**: Only one grove, so singular **grove**.
- **[fairy|fairies]**: Faye is one fairy, so singular **fairy**.
- **[dust|dusts]**: "dust" is uncountable, so singular.
- **[flowers|flower]**: She sprinkles magic on many, so plural **flowers**.
- **[colors-color]**: Both forms work; flowers bloom into vibrant color or colors.
- **[animals|animal]**: Many animals, so plural **animals**.
- **[squirrel|squirrels]**: She found one squirrel, so singular **squirrel**.
- **[acorns-acorn]**: Both forms acceptable; the squirrel lost one or many acorns.
- **[trees-tree]** and **[nuts-nut]**: Both forms work; she grew one or many.
- **[smile-smiles]**: The squirrel thanked her with a big smile or smiles; both are correct.
- **[creatures-creature]**: Both forms acceptable; she helps one or many creatures.

Heartwarming, isn't it? ğŸŒŸ

### Item 6 (ID: mermaid)
**English**: # ğŸ§œâ€â™€ï¸ Let's learn singular and plural with Marina!

- **[ocean|oceans]**: Referring to one specific ocean, use singular **ocean**.
- **[mermaid|mermaids]**: Marina is one mermaid, so use singular **mermaid**.
- **[shells|shell]**: She collected many shells, so plural **shells**.
- **[pearls|pearl]**: "Ten" means more than one, so plural **pearls**.
- **[starfish|starfishes]**: "Five" means more than one, so plural **starfishes**.
- **[comb|combs]**: She found one comb, so singular **comb**.
- **[ship-ships]**: A sunken ship; either singular or plural works.
- **[discovery|discoveries]**: One discovery, so singular **discovery**.
- **[turtle|turtles]**: Met one turtle, so singular **turtle**.
- **[friends-friend]**: Becoming friends usually uses plural **friends**.
- **[reef-reefs]**: Exploring multiple reefs, so plural is fitting.
- **[treasure-treasures]**: Treasure can be singular or plural.
- **[companion-companions]**: Shared with one companion, so singular **companion**.

### Item 7 (ID: giant)
**English**: # ğŸ‘¹ A story about a gentle giant and nouns!

- **[cloud|clouds]**: Above the clouds, plural **clouds** is common.
- **[giant|giants]**: Barnaby is one giant, so singular **giant**.
- **[vegetables|vegetable]**: He grew many vegetables, so plural **vegetables**.
- **[cows|cow]**: "Three" means plural, so **cows**.
- **[milk|milks]**: "Milk" is uncountable, so singular form.
- **[morning|mornings]**: One particular morning, so singular **morning**.
- **[boy|boys]**: Saw one boy, so singular **boy**.
- **[beanstalk|beanstalks]**: One beanstalk, so singular **beanstalk**.
- **[child|children]**: Refers to one child, so singular **child**.
- **[potato|potatoes]**: One large potato, so singular **potato**.
- **[home|homes]**: Returned to his one home, so singular **home**.

### Item 8 (ID: phoenix)
**English**: # ğŸ¦ The phoenix's feathers and nouns!

- **[nest|nests]**: In one nest, so singular **nest**.
- **[phoenix|phoenixes]**: One phoenix, so singular **phoenix**.
- **[feathers|feather]**: Left many feathers, so plural **feathers**.
- **[feather|feathers]**: "Each" is followed by singular **feather**.
- **[bird|birds]**: Heal one bird, so singular **bird**.
- **[healer|healers]**: One healer, so singular **healer**.
- **[feathers|feather]**: "Two" means plural **feathers**.
- **[pet|pets]**: Help his pet (singular), so **pet**.
- **[bird|birds]**: That specific bird, so singular **bird**.
- **[song|songs]**: One sweet song, so singular **song**.
- **[joy|joys]**: "Joy" is uncountable, so singular.
- **[heart|hearts]**: He has one heart, so singular **heart**.

### Item 9 (ID: wizard)
**English**: # ğŸ§™â€â™‚ï¸ The wise wizard and his nouns!

- **[tower|towers]**: In one tall tower, so singular **tower**.
- **[wizard|wizards]**: One wizard, so singular **wizard**.
- **[books|book]**: Studied many books, so plural **books**.
- **[wands|wand]**: "Many" means plural **wands**.
- **[potions|potion]**: "Several" means plural **potions**.
- **[night|nights]**: One specific night, so singular **night**.
- **[spell|spells]**: Cast one spell, so singular **spell**.
- **[star|stars]**: Create one star, so singular **star**.
- **[room|rooms]**: Lit up his one room, so singular **room**.
- **[wisdom|wisdoms]**: "Wisdom" is uncountable, so singular.
- **[student|students]**: Shared with students (plural), so **students**.

### Item 11 (ID: centaur)
**English**: # ğŸ¹ The swift centaur and his nouns!

- **[meadow|meadows]**: Through the meadow, singular **meadow** is common.
- **[centaur|centaurs]**: One centaur, so singular **centaur**.
- **[bow|bows]**: With his one bow, so singular **bow**.
- **[arrows|arrow]**: "Twelve" refers to plural **arrows**.
- **[quiver|quivers]**: In his one quiver, so singular **quiver**.
- **[deer|deers]**: Saw one deer; "deer" is its own plural, so **deer** is key here.
- **[lake|lakes]**: Near the lake, singular **lake**.
- **[runner|runners]**: He is one runner, so singular **runner**.
- **[wind|winds]**: "Wind" as a natural force is usually singular.
- **[face|faces]**: On his one face, so singular **face**.

### Item 14 (ID: yeti)
**English**: # â›„ The yeti and his snowballs!

- **[mountain|mountains]**: In the mountains, plural **mountains** is common.
- **[yeti|yetis]**: One yeti, so singular **yeti**.
- **[snowballs|snowball]**: Threw many snowballs, so plural **snowballs**.
- **[feet|foot]**: He has two feet, so plural **feet**.
- **[fur|furs]**: "Fur" is usually uncountable, so use singular form.
- **[day|days]**: One particular day, so singular **day**.
- **[snowman|snowmen]**: Made one big snowman, so singular **snowman**.
- **[carrot|carrots]**: Use one carrot, so singular **carrot**.
- **[face|faces]**: On the snowman's face, singular **face**.
- **[nose|noses]**: As one nose, so singular **nose**.

### Item 15 (ID: kraken)
**English**: # ğŸ™ The mighty kraken and its nouns!

- **[wave|waves]**: Under the waves, plural **waves**.
- **[kraken|krakens]**: One kraken, so singular **kraken**.
- **[tentacles|tentacle]**: "Ten" means plural **tentacles**.
- **[cave-caves]**: Deep caves; either singular or plural works.
- **[fish|fishes]**: "Many fish"; "fish" can be its own plural, so **fish** is standard.
- **[time|times]**: One instance, so singular **time**.
- **[submarine|submarines]**: Saw one submarine, so singular **submarine**.
- **[arm|arms]**: Waved its arms (plural), so **arms**.
- **[darkness|darknesses]**: "Darkness" is uncountable, so use singular form.

## subjunctive_mood.json

### Item 1
**English**: Second conditional uses subjunctive 'were'.

**Traditional**: ç¬¬äºŒæ¢ä»¶å¥ä½¿ç”¨è™›æ“¬èªæ°£ 'were'ã€‚

**Simplified**: ç¬¬äºŒæ¡ä»¶å¥ä½¿ç”¨è™šæ‹Ÿè¯­æ°” 'were'ã€‚

### Item 2
**English**: Use 'were' instead of 'was' for hypothetical wishes.

**Traditional**: å‡è¨­æ€§é¡˜æœ›ä½¿ç”¨ 'were' è€Œé 'was'ã€‚

**Simplified**: å‡è®¾æ€§æ„¿æœ›ä½¿ç”¨ 'were' è€Œé 'was'ã€‚

---

### Item 3

**Traditional**: å»ºè­°é¡å‹•è©å¾Œæ¥åŸå½¢å‹•è©ã€‚

**Simplified**: å»ºè®®ç±»åŠ¨è¯åæ¥åŸå½¢åŠ¨è¯ã€‚

---

### Item 4

**Traditional**: 'Important that' ä¹‹å¾Œä½¿ç”¨åŸå½¢å‹•è©ã€‚

**Simplified**: 'Important that' ä¹‹åä½¿ç”¨åŸå½¢åŠ¨è¯ã€‚

## transitive_intransitive.json

### Item 1 (ID: ti1)
**English**: Transitive verbs need an object; Intransitive verbs do not.
1. **slept**: Intransitive.
2. **bought**: Transitive.
3. **arrived**: Intransitive.
4. **took**: Transitive.
5. **cried**: Intransitive.

**Traditional**: åŠç‰©å‹•è© (Transitive) éœ€è¦å—è©ï¼›ä¸åŠç‰©å‹•è© (Intransitive) ä¸éœ€è¦ã€‚

4. **took**: åŠç‰©ï¼Œæ‹¿ pizzaã€‚
5. **cried**: ä¸åŠç‰©ï¼Œä¸æ¥å—è©ã€‚

**Simplified**: åŠç‰©åŠ¨è¯ (Transitive) éœ€è¦å®¾è¯­ï¼›ä¸åŠç‰©åŠ¨è¯ (Intransitive) ä¸éœ€è¦ã€‚
1. **slept**: ä¸åŠç‰©ï¼Œä¸å¯ç›´æ¥æ¥åè¯ã€‚
2. **bought**: åŠç‰©ï¼Œä¹°â€œä»€ä¹ˆâ€ï¼Ÿä¹° a new carã€‚
3. **arrived**: ä¸åŠç‰©ï¼Œä¸å¯ç›´æ¥æ¥å®¾è¯­ã€‚
4. **took**: åŠç‰©ï¼Œæ‹¿ pizzaã€‚

## verbs.json

### Item 1 (ID: baker)
**English**: # ğŸ‘¨â€ğŸ³ The Busy Baker Ben (Third Person Singular)

This story describes a routine. When the subject is **He**, **She**, or **It**, we usually add 's' or 'es' to the verb!

1. **[wakes]**: He wakes up. (Base: wake)
2. **[mixes]**: He mixes. (Ends in 'x', so add 'es')
3. **[kneads]**: He kneads the dough.
4. **[bakes]**: He bakes the bread.
5. **[smells]**: The bakery (It) smells good.
6. **[arrive]**: Customers (They) arrive. (Plural subject, no 's')
7. **[sells]**: Ben (He) sells pastries.
8. **[cleans]**: He cleans up.
9. **[rests]**: He rests.
10. **[loves]**: He loves his job.

**Traditional**: # ğŸ‘¨â€ğŸ³ å¿™ç¢Œçš„éºµåŒ…å¸« Ben (ç¬¬ä¸‰äººç¨±å–®æ•¸)

### Item 2 (ID: puppy)
**English**: # ğŸ¶ The Lost Puppy (Past Tense)

This happened **yesterday**, so we use the **Past Tense** for all verbs.

1. **[found]**: Irregular past of 'find'.
2. **[looked]**: Regular past (add -ed).
3. **[shivered]**: Regular past (shiver -> shivered).
4. **[picked]**: Regular past.
5. **[carried]**: Regular past (carry -> carried).
6. **[gave]**: Irregular past of 'give'.
7. **[drank]**: Irregular past of 'drink'.
8. **[wagged]**: Regular past (wag -> wagged).
9. **[named]**: Regular past (name -> named).
10. **[became]**: Irregular past of 'become'.

**Traditional**: # ğŸ¶ è¿·è·¯çš„å°ç‹— (éå»å¼)

7. **[drank]**ï¼šdrink çš„éå»å¼ (ä¸è¦å‰‡)ã€‚

9. **[named]**ï¼šname + dã€‚

**Simplified**: # ğŸ¶ è¿·è·¯çš„å°ç‹— (è¿‡å»å¼)

### Item 3 (ID: garden)
**English**: # ğŸŒ» Garden Life (Simple Present)

We are identifying facts and current states. Watch out for Singular vs. Plural subjects!

1. **[shines]**: Sun (it) shines.
2. **[grow]**: Seeds (they) grow.
3. **[falls]**: Rain (it) falls.
4. **[need]**: Plants (they) need.
5. **[blooms]**: A flower (it) blooms.

### Item 15 (ID: winter)
**English**: # â„ï¸ Winter Season (Simple Present)

6. [drink]: We drink
7. [become]: Days become
